## 1. The National Opportunity

### India's Structural Energy Vulnerability

| National Metric | Data |
|---|---|
| LPG consumption (2024–25) | 33.15 MMT |
| Imported LPG share | ~60% |
| Import route vulnerability | ~90% through Strait of Hormuz |
| Annual LPG subsidy burden | ₹30,000+ crore |
| Households dependent on LPG | ~300 million |
| Biogas plants in India | 4.9 million |
| SATAT CBG plants operational (target 5,000) | ~130+ |
| Total organic waste (annual, untreated) | ~700 million tonnes |
| Current utilisation of organic waste | <2% |
| SATAT guaranteed CBG floor price | ₹46/kg |

### YAROK14's Core Technical Advantage

| Metric | Conventional | YAROK14 Optimised | Improvement |
|---|---|---|---|
| Total cycle time | 46–112 days | ~6 days | Up to 18× faster |
| Daily gas output (2 m³ digester) | 0.6–1.0 m³/day | 1.5–2.5 m³/day | ~2.5× higher |
| Methane content | 55–65% | 60–70% | Improved |
| Monitoring | None | Real-time SCADA, 24/7 | Full intelligence |
| Energy overhead | Uncontrolled | Capped at ≤10% of prior day's net output | Financially disciplined |

### Mandatory CBG Blending — A Policy-Backed Demand Curve

| Financial Year | Mandatory Blending % in CNG/PNG |
|---|---|
| FY 2025–26 | 1% |
| FY 2026–27 | 3% |
| FY 2027–28 | 4% |
| FY 2028–29 onwards | 5% |

YAROK14 plants sell directly into this government-created demand. The biogas sector is only profitable when 4 things are controlled well — cheap feedstock, high uptime, full monetisation of all outputs, and reduced CapEx via subsidies. YAROK14's system is designed specifically to guarantee all four.

## 2. Core Financial Terms — Applied to YAROK14

This section defines every financial term used in this report, with YAROK14-specific context applied to each.

### 1) CapEx — Capital Expenditure
**Meaning:** One-time initial setup cost.

In YAROK14, CapEx includes: digester tank, civil works, piping, gas holder, H₂S scrubber, moisture trap, compressor/purifier, sensors + controller + SCADA (YAROK14 system), electrical panel, installation and commissioning.

### 2) OpEx — Operating Expenditure
**Meaning:** Yearly/monthly running cost.

In YAROK14, OpEx includes: labor, feedstock transport, electricity, water, maintenance, chemicals/pH correction, filter media replacement, sensor calibration, repairs, AMC/service, insurance.

### 3) Revenue
**Meaning:** Total money earned from all output streams.

Revenue streams in biogas: biogas sales, Bio-CNG/CBG sales, electricity/thermal energy savings, LPG/diesel replacement savings, organic manure/digestate sales, waste tipping fee, carbon credits (optional).

### 4) Gross Profit
$$\text{Gross Profit} = \text{Revenue} - \text{Direct Operating Cost}$$
Income before full overheads and finance costs.

### 5) Net Profit
$$\text{Net Profit} = \text{Revenue} - \text{Total OpEx}$$
If including loan, depreciation, and taxes:
$$\text{Net Profit After Tax} = \text{Revenue} - \text{OpEx} - \text{Interest} - \text{Depreciation} - \text{Tax}$$

**Simple profitability rule:** A biogas plant is profitable when:
> Annual Revenue + Annual Savings > OpEx + Loan EMI + Depreciation burden

### 6) ROI — Return on Investment ⭐
$$\text{ROI} = \frac{\text{Annual Net Profit}}{\text{Initial Investment}} \times 100$$

Higher ROI = better project attractiveness. For YAROK14's pitch:
> *"We improve plant ROI from ~15–20% to ~25–35% by increasing methane yield, uptime, and energy efficiency."*

### 7) Payback Period
$$\text{Payback Period} = \frac{\text{Initial Investment}}{\text{Annual Net Cash Inflow}}$$

Quick conversion rule:
| Annual ROI | Approximate Payback |
|---|---|
| 10% | 10 years |
| 20% | 5 years |
| 25% | 4 years |
| 33% | 3 years |
| 50% | 2 years |

### 8) Break-even Point (BEP)
The point where total income = total cost. Can be expressed in: years of operation, m³ gas/day, tonnes/day feedstock, or ₹ sales/year.

### 9) Cash Flow
Actual money moving in and out over time. Important: **Profit ≠ Cash Flow** always, because of loan repayment, depreciation, delayed payments, replacement costs.

$$\text{Net Cash Inflow} = \text{Revenue} - \text{Cash Operating Cost}$$

### 10) EBITDA ⭐ (Advanced — very investor-friendly)
**Earnings Before Interest, Taxes, Depreciation, and Amortization**
$$\text{EBITDA} = \text{Revenue} - \text{Operating Expenses (excluding D\&A)}$$

Shows the **true operating performance** of the plant. Heavily used in investor decks.

### 11) EBIT
**Earnings Before Interest and Tax**
$$\text{EBIT} = \text{Revenue} - \text{OpEx} - \text{Depreciation}$$

### 12) Depreciation
Spreading equipment cost over useful life.

For YAROK14 plants:
- Digester (RCC): 20–30 year life → depreciation over 15–20 years for financial modelling
- Control electronics / YAROK14 SCADA system: 5–10 years
- Sensors (pH, gas, temp): 1–5 years

Example: Digester + equipment = ₹50 lakh, useful life = 10 years → Depreciation = ₹5 lakh/year

### 13) IRR — Internal Rate of Return ⭐
The discount rate at which NPV = 0. Higher IRR = better project attractiveness.

| IRR | Interpretation |
|---|---|
| <10% | Weak |
| 12–18% | Acceptable |
| 18–25% | Good |
| 25%+ | Strong / Attractive |

Industry sources suggest 14–20% IRR for well-run Indian CBG projects. A 2024 scientific case study reported ~37.13% annual ROI with ~31 months payback for a best-case optimised CBG scenario.

### 14) NPV — Net Present Value ⭐
$$\text{NPV} = \sum \frac{\text{Cash Flow}_t}{(1+r)^t} - \text{Initial Investment}$$

- NPV > 0 → project is financially good
- NPV < 0 → not attractive

Discount rate typically used in India: 10–15%.

### 15) DCF — Discounted Cash Flow
Method of valuing a project using future cash flows discounted to today. Very professional term for investor decks, bankable project reports, and grant applications.

### 16) DSCR — Debt Service Coverage Ratio ⭐ (Critical for banks)
$$\text{DSCR} = \frac{\text{Net Operating Income}}{\text{Debt Service}}$$

Rule: DSCR >1.2 = usually safe; >1.5 = strong. Banks require this before lending.

### 17) Specific Gas Yield (Biogas-specific)
$$\text{Specific Gas Yield} = \frac{\text{m}^3 \text{ biogas produced}}{\text{kg feedstock or kg VS}}$$

Both a technical and financial metric. Higher yield = more revenue from same feedstock.

### 18) Methane Yield (YAROK14's core KPI)
$$\text{Methane Yield} = \frac{\text{m}^3 \text{ CH}_4}{\text{kg VS added}}$$

This is the killer performance indicator for YAROK14's optimization system.

### 19) Capacity Utilisation / Plant Load Factor (PLF)
$$\text{Capacity Utilisation} = \frac{\text{Actual Output}}{\text{Rated Output}} \times 100$$

Example: Rated 100 m³/day, Actual 82 m³/day → Utilisation = 82%

### 20) Uptime / Availability
$$\text{Uptime} = \frac{\text{Operating Time}}{\text{Total Time}} \times 100$$

For YAROK14: this is a huge business metric. A plant running 85–90% uptime vs 70% uptime can change the entire financial model.

### 21) LCOG — Levelized Cost of Gas
$$\text{LCOG} = \frac{\text{Total Lifetime Cost (discounted)}}{\text{Total Lifetime Gas Output (discounted)}}$$

Very powerful for professional reports comparing YAROK14-optimised vs conventional plants.

### 22) Profitability Ratios
$$\text{Gross Margin} = \frac{\text{Gross Profit}}{\text{Revenue}} \times 100$$
$$\text{Net Profit Margin} = \frac{\text{Net Profit}}{\text{Revenue}} \times 100$$
$$\text{Operating Margin} = \frac{\text{EBITDA or EBIT}}{\text{Revenue}} \times 100$$

### 23) Debt-Equity Ratio
$$\text{D/E Ratio} = \frac{\text{Debt}}{\text{Equity}}$$

Example: Loan = ₹30 lakh, Owner equity = ₹20 lakh → D/E = 1.5

## 3. CapEx — Project Cost Breakdown

### Small Unit — 2 m³ Digester (Household / Community)

| Component | Min (₹) | Max (₹) |
|---|---|---|
| Digester tank (GI/FRP) | 25,000 | 60,000 |
| Air jacket outer shell | 8,000 | 15,000 |
| Insulation materials | 3,000 | 8,000 |
| Black thermal coating | 500 | 1,500 |
| **YAROK14 Control Board — Prototype (MSP430 + ESP8266)** | **3,000** | **5,000** |
| **YAROK14 Control Board — MuP v2 ASIC (roadmap)** | **1,500** | **2,500** |
| Temperature sensors DS18B20 ×3 | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| pH sensor + amplifier | 1,500 | 3,500 |
| Pressure sensor | 500 | 1,500 |
| MQ-4 gas sensor | 200 | 500 |
| Energy meter | 1,000 | 2,500 |
| Agitator motor + driver | 3,000 | 8,000 |
| Heating element (immersion) | 2,000 | 5,000 |
| SSR (Solid State Relay) | 500 | 1,200 |
| pH dosing pumps ×2 | 1,600 | 5,000 |
| Pressure relief valve | 500 | 1,500 |
| Gas outlet valve (solenoid) | 800 | 2,000 |
| SPM membrane module | 15,000 | 35,000 |
| Gas storage bag (200–500L) | 2,000 | 5,000 |
| Piping, fittings, valves | 3,000 | 8,000 |
| Wi-Fi router | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| Power supply (SMPS) | 1,000 | 2,500 |
| Wiring, connectors, enclosure | 2,000 | 4,000 |
| Solar panel (100W) | 3,500 | 6,000 |
| Solar charge controller | 1,500 | 3,000 |
| Battery (100Ah) | 7,000 | 12,000 |
| Foundation and mounting | 2,000 | 5,000 |
| Installation and commissioning | 8,000 | 15,000 |
| Initial feedstock inoculum | 1,000 | 3,000 |
| **TOTAL CapEx (without solar, prototype)** | **₹91,200** | **₹1,80,200** |
| **TOTAL CapEx (with solar, prototype)** | **₹1,03,200** | **₹2,01,200** |
| **TOTAL CapEx (MuP v2 ASIC, no solar)** | **₹89,700** | **₹1,77,700** |

### Medium Unit — 10 m³ Digester (Institutional Scale)

| Component | Estimated CapEx (₹) |
|---|---|
| Digester tank (RCC or FRP, 10 m³) | 1,50,000 – 3,00,000 |
| YAROK14 control system (scaled) | 15,000 – 25,000 |
| Larger agitator (0.5–1 kW) | 10,000 – 20,000 |
| Industrial heating system (2–5 kW) | 15,000 – 30,000 |
| Gas compressor (for storage) | 25,000 – 60,000 |
| All other components (scaled) | 50,000 – 1,00,000 |
| Installation | 30,000 – 60,000 |
| **TOTAL** | **₹2.95 lakh – ₹5.95 lakh** |

### CapEx Rule for YAROK14

> *"Profitability is not maximised by the largest digester, but by the correctly sized digester operating at optimal loading, retention time, and uptime."*

**Digester Volume = Daily Slurry Input × HRT**

Where HRT (Hydraulic Retention Time) = 6 days in YAROK14's optimised system (vs 30–60 days conventional). This means YAROK14 can produce the same daily gas output from a **5–10× smaller tank** — dramatically reducing CapEx.

### Subsidy Stacking — Maximum Capital Relief

| Scheme | Amount per Plant (₹) |
|---|---|
| MNRE National Biogas Programme | ₹10,000 – ₹50,000 |
| ANERT Kerala state subsidy | ₹15,000 – ₹30,000 |
| PMEGP (35% rural subsidy) | Up to ₹1,57,500 |
| **Maximum combined subsidy (3 plants)** | **Up to ₹7.12 lakh** |

Maximum subsidy stacking can cover **100–200% of CapEx** — making the project effectively zero-capital for communities.

## 5. Revenue Model — All Streams

A lot of plants fail because they only think about "gas." YAROK14's model captures all four revenue streams simultaneously.

### Revenue Stack

| Stream | Small Site (₹/year) | Institutional (₹/year) | Railway/Large (₹/year) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Gas sales / LPG replacement savings | 12,000 – 40,000 | 75,000 – 2,50,000 | 3,00,000 – 15,00,000 |
| Waste disposal tipping fee | 8,000 – 35,000 | 40,000 – 1,20,000 | 2,00,000 – 10,00,000 |
| Digestate / organic manure sales | 5,000 – 20,000 | 15,000 – 60,000 | 50,000 – 3,00,000 |
| Carbon credits (optional) | 13,650 – 40,950 | 50,000 – 1,50,000 | 1,50,000 – 5,00,000 |
| **Total Annual Revenue/Savings** | **₹38,650 – ₹1,35,950** | **₹1.80 lakh – ₹5.80 lakh** | **₹7.0 lakh – ₹33.0 lakh** |

### Why Tipping Fees Matter

If the site charges a **waste disposal / tipping fee** (as municipal and institutional waste-based plants do), profit increases dramatically. Municipal and industrial waste-based plants outperform farm-only plants for this reason. The Brahmapuram CBG plant in Kochi (150 TPD) is structured exactly on this integrated model — CBG + digestate + tipping fee.

### SATAT CBG Offtake

For plants that scale to CBG grade (>90% CH₄, compressed):

| Metric | Value |
|---|---|
| SATAT floor price | ₹46/kg CBG |
| Example: 5 TPD Bio-CNG plant output | ~50 kg CBG/day |
| Monthly CBG revenue | 50 × 30 × ₹46 = **₹69,000/month** |
| Annual CBG revenue | **₹8.28 lakh/year** |

Plus carbon credits, fertiliser, and tipping fee on top.

## 6. Profitability Analysis

### Simple Profitability Check (All Site Types)

| Site Type | Annual Revenue | Annual OpEx | Annual Net Profit | Net Margin |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Small (2 m³, conservative) | ₹38,650 | ₹37,900 | ₹750 | ~2% |
| Small (2 m³, optimistic) | ₹1,35,950 | ₹1,09,500 | ₹26,450 | ~19% |
| Small (2 m³, free feedstock + tipping fee) | ₹1,35,950 | ₹25,900 | ₹1,10,050 | ~81% |
| Institutional (10 m³) | ₹3,30,000 | ₹3,19,000 | ₹11,000 | ~3% |
| Institutional (optimised, all streams) | ₹5,80,000 | ₹3,00,000 | ₹2,80,000 | ~48% |
| Railway / large | ₹20,00,000 | ₹8,00,000 | ₹12,00,000 | ~60% |

**Key insight:** Plants become highly profitable when:
1. Feedstock is free (cow dung, food waste, market waste)
2. Tipping fees are charged for waste disposal
3. All three revenue streams are monetised (gas + manure + carbon)
4. YAROK14 optimization improves uptime to 85–95%

### Profitability Impact of YAROK14 Optimisation

Even modest improvements from YAROK14 change ROI dramatically:

| Optimization Gain | Effect |
|---|---|
| +10–20% gas yield | More revenue from same feedstock |
| +5–10% uptime | More operating days, less downtime loss |
| −10–15% parasitic power | Lower electricity OpEx |
| Lower pH crash downtime | Avoided revenue loss (each pH crash = 1–3 days loss) |
| Better digestate quality | Higher organic manure sale price |

## 7. ROI Analysis

### ROI Formula Applied to YAROK14

$$\text{ROI} = \frac{\text{Annual Net Profit}}{\text{Initial Investment}} \times 100$$

### Typical ROI by Plant Type

| Plant Type | Without Optimization | With YAROK14 Optimization |
|---|---|---|
| Small household / farm | 10–25% | 20–35%+ |
| Medium / community / commercial | 15–30% (well-run), <10% (poorly run) | 25–40% |
| CBG / Bio-CNG / municipal | 14–25% | 25–40%+ |
| Best-case integrated projects | — | 30%+ |

### YAROK14 Investor ROI Pitch

Example: A plant with ROI = 18% before YAROK14 can become:

| Improvement | Result |
|---|---|
| Methane yield +12% | +₹X revenue |
| Uptime +8% | +₹X revenue |
| Parasitic power −10% | −₹X OpEx |
| **Combined new ROI** | **25–32%** |

> *"That's a huge jump — and a very investable story."*

### Small Site ROI Example

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| CapEx (with subsidies) | ₹85,000 |
| Annual net benefit | ₹20,000 |
| **ROI** | **₹20,000 / ₹85,000 × 100 = 23.5% per year** |

### Institutional Site ROI Example

| Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| CapEx | ₹3,75,000 (after ₹75,000 subsidy) |
| Annual net saving | ₹2,80,000 |
| **ROI** | **₹2,80,000 / ₹3,75,000 × 100 = 74.7% per year** |

## 8. Payback Period Analysis

$$\text{Payback Period} = \frac{\text{Initial Investment}}{\text{Annual Net Cash Inflow}}$$

### Payback by Scenario

| Scenario | CapEx (₹) | Subsidies (₹) | Net CapEx (₹) | Annual Benefit (₹) | Payback |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2 m³, no subsidy | 1,50,000 | 0 | 1,50,000 | 7,210–17,800 | 8–21 months |
| 2 m³, MNRE only | 1,50,000 | 35,000 | 1,15,000 | 7,210–17,800 | 6–16 months |
| 2 m³, MNRE + ANERT | 1,50,000 | 65,000 | 85,000 | 7,210–17,800 | 5–12 months |
| 2 m³, all subsidies | 1,50,000 | 1,10,250 | 39,750 | 7,210–17,800 | **2–6 months** |
| 10 m³ institutional | 4,50,000 | 75,000 | 3,75,000 | 24,500–44,500 | 8–15 months |
| 10 m³, all subsidies | 4,50,000 | 2,00,000 | 2,50,000 | 24,500–44,500 | 6–10 months |

### Industry Benchmarks (for credibility)

| Plant Type | Typical Payback (India) | With YAROK14 Optimization |
|---|---|---|
| Small household / farm | 3–8 years (published Indian studies) | 2.5–5 years |
| Commercial CBG / Bio-CNG | 4–6 years | 2.5–4 years |
| Optimised + strong feedstock + manure revenue | 2.5–4 years | 2–3 years |

**One-line answer:** Break-even time is usually ~3–6 years; with strong optimization it can become ~2.5–4 years.

### Post-Payback Profit Window

For a plant with 4-year payback and 20-year life:
- 16 years of productive operation remain after payback
- Minus maintenance / replacements
- This is where the **real lifetime profit** comes from

Plant economic life for ROI models: **15–20 years**
Plant physical life (well-built RCC digester): **20–30 years**

If CapEx = ₹10 lakh, payback = 4 years, life = 20 years:
→ **16 years of post-payback benefit = massive lifetime ROI**

## 9. IRR and NPV

### IRR Reference for YAROK14 Plants

| Plant Type | Typical IRR |
|---|---|
| Small household | 15–25% |
| Well-optimised community | 20–35% |
| Commercial CBG | 14–20% |
| Best-case optimised CBG (2024 case study) | ~37% |

### NPV Example — Institutional Site (10 m³)

Assumptions:
- CapEx: ₹3,75,000
- Annual net cash flow: ₹2,80,000
- Discount rate: 12%
- Life: 15 years

$$\text{NPV} = \sum_{t=1}^{15} \frac{2,80,000}{(1.12)^t} - 3,75,000$$

NPV ≈ **₹16.7 lakh** (strongly positive → excellent project)

### 20-Year Cash Flow Summary — Small Site (Optimistic)

| Period | Event | Cumulative Net (₹) |
|---|---|---|
| Year 0 | CapEx (after subsidies): -₹39,750 | -39,750 |
| Year 1 | Net benefit: +₹17,800 | -21,950 |
| Year 2 | Net benefit: +₹17,800 | -4,150 |
| Year 2.25 | **Break-even** | 0 |
| Years 3–20 | ₹17,800/year × 17.75 years | **+₹3,15,950** |
| **Lifetime profit (20 years)** | | **~₹2,76,200** |

## 10. Before vs After YAROK14 Optimization

This is the most powerful single slide for YAROK14's investor pitch.

### Before vs After — 2 m³ Small Site

| Metric | Before (Conventional) | After (YAROK14) | Change |
|---|---|---|---|
| Daily gas output | 0.6–1.0 m³/day | 1.5–2.5 m³/day | +150–250% |
| Methane content | 55–65% | 60–70% | +5% |
| Cycle time | 46–112 days | ~6 days | 18× faster |
| Uptime | 60–75% | 85–95% | +20–30% |
| pH crash events | Multiple per year | Near zero | Eliminated |
| Operator skill required | High | Low | Reduced |
| SCADA monitoring | None | 24/7 real-time | Full intelligence |
| Annual gas value | ₹12,000–₹25,000 | ₹40,000–₹80,000 | 2–3× |
| Annual net profit | Low / negative | ₹20,000–₹80,000+ | Transformed |
| ROI | 5–15% | 20–35%+ | Doubled+ |
| Payback | 5–8 years | 2–4 years | Halved |

### Before vs After — 10 m³ Institutional

| Metric | Before (Conventional) | After (YAROK14) | Change |
|---|---|---|---|
| Monthly gas saving | ₹15,000–₹25,000 | ₹57,000–₹85,000 | 3–4× |
| Annual LPG cost saved | ₹1.8–₹3 lakh | ₹5–₹8 lakh | 3× |
| Plant uptime | ~70% | 85–95% | +15–25% |
| Failed cycles/year | 4–8 | 0–1 | Eliminated |
| Annual net profit | ₹0–₹50,000 | ₹2–₹4 lakh | Transformed |
| Payback period | 10–15 years | 4–8 months | 15× faster |

### The TERI Validation

A January 2025 TERI study of 11 SATAT plants found: 73% had no monitoring system, 73% had silent production loss of up to 30%, and all 11 had insufficient operator knowledge. YAROK14 eliminates all three problems.

## 11. Unit Economics

### Cost per m³ Biogas — YAROK14 vs Conventional

$$\text{Unit Cost} = \frac{\text{Annual Total Cost}}{\text{Annual Biogas Production}}$$

| Plant Configuration | Annual Cost (₹) | Annual Output (m³) | Cost per m³ (₹) |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2 m³ conventional | 50,000 | 219–365 | 137–228 |
| 2 m³ YAROK14 optimised | 50,000 | 548–913 | 55–91 |
| 10 m³ institutional (conventional) | 3,00,000 | 2,190–3,650 | 82–137 |
| 10 m³ YAROK14 optimised | 3,00,000 | 5,475–9,125 | 33–55 |

YAROK14 roughly **halves the cost per m³** through higher yield at same OpEx.

### Cost per kg CBG (for SATAT grade)

$$\text{Cost per kg CBG} = \frac{\text{Annual Total Cost}}{\text{Annual CBG Output}}$$

Typical SATAT floor price = ₹46/kg. For profitability: cost per kg CBG must be <₹40.

### Methane Yield — YAROK14's Core KPI

$$\text{Methane Yield} = \frac{\text{m}^3 \text{ CH}_4}{\text{kg VS added}}$$

| Feedstock | Conventional Yield | YAROK14 Optimised |
|---|---|---|
| Cattle dung | 0.15–0.20 m³/kg VS | 0.22–0.28 m³/kg VS |
| Kitchen/food waste | 0.25–0.35 m³/kg VS | 0.38–0.48 m³/kg VS |
| Mixed (cattle + kitchen) | 0.18–0.28 m³/kg VS | 0.28–0.42 m³/kg VS |

### Capacity Utilisation Example

| Configuration | Rated Output | YAROK14 Actual | Utilisation |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2 m³ unit | 2.0 m³/day | 1.8 m³/day | 90% |
| 10 m³ unit | 10.0 m³/day | 8.8 m³/day | 88% |

## 15. KPI Reference Set

### Recommended 12 KPIs for YAROK14 Project Reporting

Use these in every investor deck, grant application, and bankable project report:

| # | KPI | Formula / Unit |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | CapEx | ₹ (total) |
| 2 | Annual OpEx | ₹/year |
| 3 | Annual Revenue | ₹/year |
| 4 | Annual Net Profit | ₹/year |
| 5 | ROI | % per year |
| 6 | Payback Period | Years |
| 7 | IRR | % |
| 8 | NPV | ₹ |
| 9 | Methane Yield | m³ CH₄/kg VS |
| 10 | Uptime | % |
| 11 | Cost per m³ biogas | ₹/m³ |
| 12 | Lifetime Profit (15–20 years) | ₹ |

### Best Report Section Headings

For any YAROK14 report, PPT, or DPR, use:

- Project Cost (CapEx)
- Operating Cost (OpEx)
- Revenue Model
- Profitability Analysis
- Break-even Analysis
- ROI Analysis
- IRR & NPV Analysis
- Cash Flow Projection (10/20 Years)
- Sensitivity Analysis
- Risk & Mitigation
- Unit Economics (₹/m³ biogas, ₹/kg CBG)
- Optimization Impact Analysis (Before vs After YAROK14)

### Investor-Grade Language

| Instead of saying... | Say... |
|---|---|
| "Our controller improves sensors" | "Our optimization platform increases methane yield, improves plant uptime, reduces specific energy consumption, lowers unit gas cost, shortens payback period, and increases project IRR." |
| "We monitor the plant" | "We improve plant ROI from ~15–20% to ~25–35% by increasing methane yield, uptime, and energy efficiency." |
| "We make biogas smarter" | "We do not build just another biogas plant. We increase profitability of existing and new plants by improving gas yield, uptime, and energy efficiency." |

---

## 16. Financial Terms Glossary

| Term | Definition | YAROK14 Application |
|---|---|---|
| **CapEx** | Capital Expenditure — one-time setup cost | ₹91,200 – ₹2,01,200 for 2 m³ unit |
| **OpEx** | Operating Expenditure — recurring costs | ₹37,900 – ₹1,09,500/year (small site) |
| **Revenue** | Total income from all output streams | Gas + manure + tipping fee + carbon credits |
| **Gross Profit** | Revenue − Direct Operating Cost | Before overheads and finance |
| **Net Profit** | Revenue − Total OpEx | After all costs |
| **ROI** | Annual Net Profit / Investment × 100 | 20–35% with YAROK14 |
| **Payback Period** | Investment / Annual Net Cash Inflow | 2–6 months (with subsidies) |
| **BEP** | Break-even Point — where income = cost | ~2.25 years (small optimistic) |
| **Cash Flow** | Actual money in/out over time | Monthly + annual + 20-year projection |
| **Net Cash Inflow** | Revenue − Cash Operating Cost | Used in payback calculation |
| **EBITDA** | Earnings Before Interest, Taxes, Depreciation, Amortization | True operating performance |
| **EBIT** | Earnings Before Interest and Tax | Revenue − OpEx − Depreciation |
| **Depreciation** | Equipment cost spread over useful life | Digester: 20-year life; YAROK14 electronics: 5–10 years |
| **IRR** | Internal Rate of Return | 14–37% depending on plant type |
| **NPV** | Net Present Value | Must be >0 for viable project |
| **DCF** | Discounted Cash Flow | For bankable project reports |
| **Discount Rate** | Rate used in NPV/DCF | 10–15% typical in India |
| **DSCR** | Debt Service Coverage Ratio | Must be >1.2 for bank loans |
| **Specific Gas Yield** | m³ biogas / kg feedstock or kg VS | Key efficiency metric |
| **Methane Yield** | m³ CH₄ / kg VS added | YAROK14's primary KPI |
| **PLF / Capacity Utilisation** | Actual / Rated Output × 100 | Target 85–95% with YAROK14 |
| **Uptime** | Operating Time / Total Time × 100 | Huge business metric for YAROK14 |
| **LCOG** | Levelized Cost of Gas | For comparing plant sizes |
| **Cost per m³** | Annual Total Cost / Annual Biogas Output | YAROK14 halves this vs conventional |
| **Cost per kg CBG** | Annual Total Cost / Annual CBG Output | Must be <₹40 for SATAT profitability |
| **Gross Margin** | Gross Profit / Revenue × 100 | Hardware: 35–47%; SaaS: 70–90% |
| **Net Profit Margin** | Net Profit / Revenue × 100 | Stage 3 (1,000 sites): 20–38% |
| **Debt** | Borrowed money (bank loan) | CGTMSE / KFC / SIDBI |
| **Equity** | Owner/investor money | Founder capital + grants |
| **D/E Ratio** | Debt / Equity | Target ≤1.5 |
| **Interest Cost** | Yearly loan interest paid | Based on loan scheme rate |
| **EMI / Debt Service** | Loan repayment burden | Monthly EMI from bank |
| **Tipping Fee** | Charge for accepting waste | Major revenue stream for institutional/railway |
| **Savings / Cost Avoidance** | Fuel/electricity/disposal cost avoided | Used instead of "revenue" for internal-use plants |
| **AMC** | Annual Maintenance Contract | YAROK14's recurring SaaS + service fee |
| **SATAT** | Sustainable Alternative Towards Affordable Transportation | CBG offtake scheme at ₹46/kg |
| **LCOE** | Levelized Cost of Energy | Equivalent metric for power generation |

---

# PART II — FROM BIOMETHANE TO SILICON
## How YAROK14's National Savings Can Finance India's 1nm Semiconductor Fab Dream

> *"The same financial discipline that makes a biogas plant profitable — CapEx reduction, OpEx control, IRR maximisation, and long-term cash flow — applies at every scale, from a 2 m³ digester in Kottayam to a $50 billion 1nm wafer fab in Dholera."*

---

## Section A — The Global Semiconductor Landscape (2025–2026 Reality)

### A.1 Where the World Stands on Advanced Nodes

| Node | Status (2026) | Key Player | Fab Cost |
|---|---|---|---|
| 28–65 nm | Mature, high volume | TSMC, Samsung, GlobalFoundries | $3–8B per fab |
| 5–7 nm | High volume production | TSMC, Samsung | $10–15B per fab |
| 3 nm | Volume production since 2023 | TSMC (Fabs 20, 22) | $15–20B per fab |
| **2 nm** | **Volume production began Q4 2025** | **TSMC (Fab 20 Hsinchu, Fab 22 Kaohsiung)** | **$20–25B per fab** |
| 1.4 nm (A14) | Under construction (Fab 25 Taichung) | TSMC | **$48.5B for 4-fab cluster** |
| **1 nm (A10)** | **R&D lines at Fab 20; 2nd phase of Fab 25** | **TSMC** | **~$60–80B estimated** |
| 0.7 nm (A7) | Planned (4th fab at Fab 20) | TSMC | R&D stage |
| Sub-0.7 nm | Hyper-NA EUV era (~2030+) | TSMC, Intel, Samsung | $100B+ range |

**Key data points (verified, 2025–2026):**
- TSMC's 1.4nm (A14) fab complex in Central Taiwan Science Park costs $48.5 billion for four fabs, with risk production targeted for late 2027 and mass production in 2028.
- At Fab 20 in Baoshan, TSMC plans the third factory for 1nm process and R&D lines, and a fourth factory possibly for 0.7nm process and R&D lines.
- TSMC Arizona's total investment reached $165 billion covering six fabs, two advanced packaging facilities, and an R&D centre — the largest FDI greenfield project in US history.
- TSMC's 2026 capital expenditure is guided at $52–56 billion, a roughly 30% year-over-year jump.

### A.2 TSMC Node Roadmap — Critical Timeline

| Year | Node / Process | Monthly Capacity Target | Wafer Price (2nm reference) |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2023 | 3 nm volume | 55,000 wpm | ~$20,000/wafer |
| 2025 | 2 nm volume begins | 45,000–50,000 wpm | ~$30,000/wafer |
| 2026 | 2 nm at 100,000+ wpm | Fab 20 + 22 + Arizona P2 | ~$30,000/wafer |
| 2027 | 1.4 nm (A14) risk production | Fab 25 Phase 1 | ~$35,000+ projected |
| 2028 | 1.4 nm mass production | 50,000 wpm (Fab 25) | TBD |
| 2029–2030 | 1 nm (A10) risk production | Fab 25 Phase 2 | TBD |
| 2030+ | Sub-1nm / Hyper-NA era | Planned | TBD |

---

## Section B — ASML Tool Economics: The Price of Printing Atoms

### B.1 ASML Machine Pricing Hierarchy (2025–2026)

ASML's machine pricing spans from $5–90 million for DUV systems (legacy technology, still 60% of unit volume with 374 machines sold in 2024) to $183–220 million for EUV (only 44 sold in 2024 but 38% of revenue), $350–400 million for High-NA EUV (enabling sub-2nm nodes), and an expected $724 million+ for Hyper-NA EUV planned for 2030 for sub-1nm processes.

| ASML Tool | Technology | Price Per Unit | Purpose | Annual Deliveries |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DUV (ArF Immersion) | 193nm light | $5M – $90M | 28nm to 90nm nodes | 374 units (2024) |
| EUV Low-NA (NXE series) | 13.5nm EUV | $183M – $220M | 7nm to 3nm | 44 units (2024) |
| **High-NA EUV (EXE series)** | **13.5nm, NA=0.55** | **$350M – $400M** | **Sub-2nm (2nm, 1.4nm, 1nm)** | **~6/year now; 20/year by 2028** |
| Hyper-NA EUV (planned ~2030) | Next-gen | $700M – $724M+ | Sub-0.7nm / Angstrom era | Production target TBD |

### B.2 What a High-NA EUV Machine Actually Is

ASML sold 44 EUV machines in 2024 with a price tag starting at $220 million; DUV machines are far cheaper, ranging from $5 million to $90 million, but ASML sold 374 of those legacy machines in 2024.

The High-NA EUV (Twinscan EXE) is not just expensive — it is physically extraordinary:

| Specification | Value |
|---|---|
| Weight | 150,000 kg (165 tons) |
| Shipping | 250 crates, chartered Antonov An-124 aircraft |
| Assembly | 250 engineers × 6 months per unit |
| Resolution | 8nm (vs 13nm for Low-NA EUV) |
| Wafer throughput | 185+ wafers/hour |
| Site preparation cost | ~$200M (power upgrades, vibration-isolated floor, ultra-pure water) |
| Annual maintenance contract | $10–15M per machine per year |
| Tool lifetime | ~15 years with upgrades |
| Mirrors (Zeiss) | 6 mirrors, each ~$70M, polished to sub-angstrom smoothness |

TSMC is said to be adopting High-NA EUV for its 1nm-class node sometime around 2030, but the company has not confirmed its exact timeline.

### B.3 How Many ASML Machines Does a 1nm Fab Need?

A full 1nm production fab (50,000 wpm capacity) requires approximately:

| Tool Type | Quantity Needed | Unit Cost | Total Cost |
|---|---|---|---|
| High-NA EUV (EXE) | 15–20 units | $380M | $5.7B – $7.6B |
| Low-NA EUV (NXE) | 10–15 units | $210M | $2.1B – $3.15B |
| ArF Immersion DUV | 40–60 units | $70M avg | $2.8B – $4.2B |
| Metrology tools (KLA, Applied) | 30–50 units | $5M–$30M avg | $0.5B – $1.5B |
| Etch / Deposition (Lam, AMAT) | 60–100 units | $5M–$20M avg | $0.6B – $2.0B |
| CMP, CVD, ALD systems | 40–80 units | $3M–$15M avg | $0.3B – $1.2B |
| **Total Equipment CapEx** | | | **~$12B – $20B** |

Equipment is typically 60–70% of total fab CapEx. The remainder covers civil construction, cleanroom, ultra-pure water systems, specialty gas supply, power infrastructure, and fit-out.

---

## Section C — Full CapEx Model: Building a 1nm Fab in India

### C.1 Global Reference Points

| Project | Node | CapEx | Location | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| TSMC Fab 25 (4-fab cluster) | 1.4 nm | $48.5B | Taichung, Taiwan | Most current real data |
| TSMC Arizona (6-fab gigafab) | 4nm → 2nm → sub-2nm | $165B total | Phoenix, USA | Includes R&D + packaging |
| Single advanced fab (TSMC Taiwan) | 2–3 nm | $20–25B | Taiwan | Benchmark |
| Intel Oregon (High-NA EUV adoption) | 1.8nm+ | $20B+ | Hillsboro, USA | First High-NA EUV user |
| Samsung Pyeongtaek P4 | 2–3 nm | ~$20B | South Korea | |
| **Estimated single 1nm fab** | **1 nm** | **~$40–60B** | **Greenfield** | **Modelled from roadmap data** |

### C.2 CapEx Breakdown — India 1nm Fab (Modelled, 50,000 wpm)

All figures in USD billions. India cost premium estimated at 15–25% vs Taiwan (vs 4–5× in USA).

| Category | Taiwan Cost | India Estimate | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Land & Site** | $0.5B | $0.2B – $0.4B | Land cheaper in India; Dholera SIR |
| **Cleanroom Construction** | $3B – $5B | $2.5B – $4.5B | ISO Class 1–3, vibration isolation |
| **Ultra-Pure Water (UPW) Systems** | $0.5B | $0.4B – $0.7B | 10M+ litres/day |
| **Power Infrastructure** | $0.8B | $0.7B – $1.2B | 200–500 MW dedicated supply |
| **Specialty Gas Supply** | $0.3B | $0.3B – $0.5B | NF₃, SiH₄, HF, N₂, O₂, Ar |
| **Lithography Equipment (ASML)** | $8B – $12B | $8B – $12B | Imported; no India premium |
| **Process Equipment (Lam, AMAT, KLA)** | $6B – $10B | $6B – $10B | Imported; no India premium |
| **Metrology & Inspection Tools** | $1B – $2B | $1B – $2B | Imported |
| **Chemical Delivery Systems** | $0.3B | $0.3B – $0.5B | |
| **IT / SCADA / MES / ERP** | $0.3B | $0.3B – $0.5B | |
| **R&D & Process Development** | $2B – $4B | $2B – $4B | Cannot be shortcut |
| **Talent Acquisition & Training** | $0.5B – $1B | $0.8B – $1.5B | India premium for rare talent |
| **Regulatory & Environmental** | $0.1B | $0.2B – $0.4B | India clearances |
| **Contingency (15%)** | $2B – $4B | $2B – $4B | Standard project contingency |
| **TOTAL** | **~$25B – $40B** | **~$25B – $43B** | |

> **India vs USA comparison:** TSMC stated that the cost of construction of buildings and facilities in the US is four to five times what an identical plant would cost in Taiwan, due to higher costs of labour, red tape, and training. These additional production costs will increase the cost of TSMC's chips made in the US to at least 50% more than Taiwan. India's labour costs are lower than the US, giving India a structural advantage for civil construction — but imported equipment (ASML, Lam, AMAT, KLA) is the same price globally.

### C.3 OpEx — Annual Running Cost of a 1nm Fab in India

| Cost Category | Annual (USD) |
|---|---|
| Electricity (200–500 MW × 8,760 hrs) | $500M – $1.5B |
| Ultra-pure water and chemicals | $200M – $400M |
| Specialty gases | $150M – $300M |
| Equipment maintenance (AMC) | $800M – $1.5B |
| ASML High-NA EUV service contracts ($12M × 18 tools) | $200M – $220M |
| Workforce (5,000–10,000 engineers + technicians) | $300M – $600M |
| Yield loss / scrap (target <5% at maturity) | $500M – $1B |
| Consumables (photoresists, CMP slurry, etc.) | $300M – $600M |
| R&D (process sustaining) | $200M – $500M |
| Logistics, IP licensing (TSMC-style) | $300M – $500M |
| **Total Annual OpEx** | **~$3.5B – $7B/year** |

### C.4 Revenue Model — 1nm Fab in India

A 50,000 wpm fab at 2nm/1.4nm price benchmarks (~$30,000–$35,000/wafer):

| Metric | Value |
|---|---|
| Monthly capacity | 50,000 wafers |
| Annual wafers (at 85% utilisation) | 510,000 wafers |
| Price per wafer (1.4nm reference) | $33,000 – $38,000 |
| **Gross Annual Revenue** | **$16.8B – $19.4B** |
| Annual OpEx | $3.5B – $7B |
| **Annual Gross Profit** | **$9.8B – $15.9B** |
| Depreciation (25-year fab life) | $1.6B – $2.4B/year |
| **EBITDA** | **$9.8B – $15.9B** |
| **Net Profit (after depreciation + tax)** | **~$7B – $12B/year** |

### C.5 ROI, IRR, Payback — 1nm India Fab

$$\text{ROI} = \frac{\text{Annual Net Profit}}{\text{CapEx}} \times 100$$

| Scenario | CapEx (USD) | Annual Net Profit | ROI | Payback |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Conservative (low utilisation, high OpEx) | $43B | $7B | 16.3% | ~6 years |
| Base case | $35B | $9B | 25.7% | ~4 years |
| Optimistic (high yield, pricing power) | $28B (with subsidies) | $12B | 42.9% | ~2.5 years |

**IRR (20-year model):** 18–28% depending on ramp speed, yield maturity, and wafer pricing.
**NPV (12% discount rate, 20-year life):** Strongly positive at base case — $40B–$80B.

---

## Section D — India's Current Semiconductor Position and the Gap to 1nm

### D.1 What India Has Approved (as of 2026)

India's approved projects include the Tata Electronics and Powerchip Semiconductor Manufacturing Corp joint venture committing ₹91,000 crore ($10.96 billion) to build a semiconductor fabrication plant in Dholera, Gujarat, with a planned capacity of 50,000 wafers per month, and Micron Technology's ₹22,516 crore ($2.71 billion) ATMP facility in Sanand, Gujarat.

| Project | Partner | Investment | Node | Location | Status |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Tata–PSMC Fab | Powerchip (Taiwan) | ₹91,000 cr ($11B) | 28–65 nm | Dholera, Gujarat | Under construction |
| Micron ATMP | Micron (USA) | ₹22,516 cr ($2.75B) | Packaging only | Sanand, Gujarat | Operational 2025 |
| CG Power–Renesas | Renesas (Japan) | ₹7,600 cr ($915M) | OSAT/packaging | Sanand, Gujarat | Under construction |
| Tata OSAT (TSAT) | Tata Electronics | ₹27,000 cr ($3.25B) | Packaging | Morigaon, Assam | Under construction |
| Kaynes Semicon | Kaynes Technology | ₹3,307 cr ($398M) | OSAT | Sanand, Gujarat | First chips shipped Oct 2025 |
| HCL–Foxconn JV | Foxconn (Taiwan) | ₹3,700 cr ($446M) | Display driver | Jewar, UP | Announced |
| SCL Mohali (modernisation) | Govt of India | ₹4,500 cr | Legacy CMOS | Mohali, Punjab | Announced Nov 2025 |
| **Total ISM 1.0 committed** | | **~₹1.6 lakh crore** | | | |

India's semiconductor incentives are now among the most attractive in the world — for an approved silicon fab worth at least $2.5 billion making 40,000 wafer starts per month, the federal government reimburses 50% of the fab cost with a state partner expected to add 20%.

### D.2 The Node Gap — Where India Is vs Where It Needs to Go

| Generation | Node Range | India Status (2026) | Global Leaders |
|---|---|---|---|
| Mature / Legacy | 90nm – 180nm | SCL Mohali (limited) | GlobalFoundries, SMIC |
| Mainstream | 28nm – 65nm | Tata–PSMC (under construction) | TSMC, Samsung, UMC |
| Advanced | 5nm – 16nm | Not yet | TSMC, Samsung |
| Leading Edge | 2nm – 3nm | Not planned | TSMC only (volume) |
| **Frontier** | **Sub-2nm / 1nm** | **Not yet on roadmap** | **TSMC (2029–2030)** |

**The honest gap:** India is approximately 15–20 years behind the global frontier in node technology. The Tata–PSMC 28nm fab is the equivalent of where TSMC was in 2011. Catching up to 1nm is a multi-decade, multi-hundred-billion-dollar project — but it is achievable with the right phased strategy.

### D.3 India's Policy Framework for Semiconductor Manufacturing

The Scheme for setting up of Semiconductor Fabs in India extends fiscal support of up to 50% of project cost on a pari-passu basis to approved applicants. For compound semiconductors and ATMP/OSAT units, the fiscal support is 50% of capital expenditure.

| Policy / Scheme | Support Level | Applicable To |
|---|---|---|
| ISM Fab Scheme | Up to 50% of project CapEx | Semiconductor fabs |
| ISM ATMP/OSAT Scheme | 50% of CapEx | Packaging and test |
| Gujarat Semiconductor Policy | +40% of CapEx (state top-up) | Gujarat-based projects |
| DLI Scheme | Up to 50% of design costs + EDA tools | Fabless / chip design |
| ECMS (April 2025) | ₹22,919 crore outlay | Components and materials |
| PLI Electronics | Production-linked | End products |
| ISM 2.0 (announced) | Equipment, materials, design IP, R&D | Next phase |
| SCL Mohali modernisation | ₹4,500 crore | Government fab |

**Combined central + state support ceiling (Gujarat):**
> 50% (ISM) + 40% of ISM amount (Gujarat) = effective support of up to **70% of CapEx** for qualifying projects.

---

## Section E — The YAROK14–Semiconductor Connection: How Biomethane Savings Fund Silicon

### E.1 The Bridge Thesis

YAROK14 is not a semiconductor company. But the **national savings generated by YAROK14's deployment at scale create the fiscal headroom for India to fund its semiconductor ambitions**. Here is how the numbers connect:

| YAROK14 National Savings | Equivalent Semiconductor Investment |
|---|---|
| ₹2,500 crore/year (conservative, 1L sites, after all costs) | Funds the annual OpEx of one SCL Mohali-scale modernised fab |
| ₹6,000 crore/year (gross, 1L sites) | = 50% of a 28nm fab CapEx per year |
| ₹25,000 crore/year (optimistic, 1L sites) | = 27% of India's entire ISM 1.0 committed budget, generated annually |
| ₹30,000 crore/year (5L sites, conservative) | = Cost of one full advanced packaging cluster |
| ₹1.25 lakh crore/year (5L sites, optimistic) | = India's entire ISM 1.0 budget, generated every single year |

**The strategic insight:**
> If India deploys 5 lakh YAROK14-enabled biogas nodes — saving ₹30,000–₹1.25 lakh crore per year — a fraction of that saving redirected as sovereign investment could finance the multi-decade semiconductor roadmap from 28nm today to 1nm by 2040.

### E.2 The Phased 20-Year India Semiconductor Roadmap (Practical)

| Phase | Years | Node Target | Required CapEx | How YAROK14 Savings Contribute |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Phase 0 — Foundation | 2024–2028 | 28–65 nm (Tata–PSMC) | $11B (largely committed) | Rural savings fund national balance of payments improvement |
| Phase 1 — Mainstream | 2028–2032 | 7–16 nm | $15B–$20B | ₹25,000 cr/year savings × 4 years = ₹1 lakh crore contribution |
| Phase 2 — Advanced | 2032–2037 | 3–5 nm | $20B–$30B | 5L site YAROK14 savings = ₹30,000–₹1,25,000 cr/year |
| Phase 3 — Leading Edge | 2037–2042 | 1.4 nm – 2 nm | $40B–$60B | Mature biomethane economy + semiconductor revenue recycling |
| Phase 4 — Frontier | 2042–2050 | 1 nm and below | $80B–$120B | Full sovereign fund + TSMC-style IP licensing revenue |

### E.3 YAROK14 → Semiconductor: The Circular Economy Model

```
Organic Waste
     ↓
YAROK14 Biomethane System
     ↓
Gas + Digestate + Carbon Credits
     ↓
₹30,000–₹1,25,000 crore/year national savings
     ↓ (redirected as sovereign capital)
Semiconductor Fab Fund
     ↓
Advanced Node Fab in India (28nm → 7nm → 2nm → 1nm)
     ↓
Chip Revenue + IP Licensing + Technology Export
     ↓
Reinvested in next-node R&D
     ↓
India as 1nm Fab Nation by 2040–2045
```

---

## Section F — The ASML Access Question: Can India Get the Tools?

### F.1 Export Control Reality (2026)

| Tool Type | India Access | Conditions |
|---|---|---|
| DUV (ArF Immersion) | ✅ Unrestricted | Standard commercial export |
| Low-NA EUV (NXE series) | ✅ Available | Export licence from Dutch government; India is a strategic partner |
| **High-NA EUV (EXE series)** | **✅ Available in principle** | **Requires Dutch + US export approval; India's strategic alignment with US/QUAD makes this feasible** |
| Hyper-NA EUV (~2030) | ⚠️ TBD | Not yet commercially available; export rules not yet set |

India's membership in the Quad (with the US, Japan, Australia) and its strong bilateral technology partnerships make it a natural beneficiary of advanced semiconductor tool exports — unlike China, which is explicitly blocked from EUV.

While Intel plans to use High-NA EUV tools with its post-18A process technology, TSMC is said to be adopting a more cautious approach and using the tech for its 1nm-class node sometime around 2030. India would be adopting 1nm at a similar timeline — meaning the export control and tool availability landscape will have matured significantly by the time India actually needs High-NA EUV at scale.

### F.2 ASML Equipment Roadmap India Should Follow

**Phase 1 (2024–2030): DUV + Low-NA EUV**
- For 28nm, 16nm, 7nm nodes
- DUV tools: $30M–$70M each — affordable at scale
- Low-NA EUV: $200M–$220M each — 10–20 units for first advanced fab
- Total lithography equipment: $3B–$5B

**Phase 2 (2030–2038): High-NA EUV adoption**
- For 2nm and 1.4nm production
- 15–20 High-NA EUV units at $380M–$400M each
- Total High-NA equipment alone: $5.7B–$8B
- Site prep for High-NA: $200M per tool location

**Phase 3 (2038–2045): Hyper-NA EUV**
- For sub-1nm / Angstrom era
- Estimated $700M–$724M+ per unit
- India would need to negotiate as a tier-1 customer alongside TSMC and Samsung

### F.3 ASML Service and Maintenance — Ongoing Cost

Beyond the $300M price tag, customers also pay $10–15M annually for maintenance, upgrades, and software optimization per EUV machine.

For a mature India fab with 18 High-NA EUV tools:
- Annual service contracts: 18 × $13M = **$234M/year**
- This must be built into the OpEx model from day one
- ASML service revenues grow at 20% annually as the installed base grows

---

## Section G — Financial Model: India's Node Progression Investment Plan

### G.1 Capital Required at Each Node — India-Specific

| Target Node | CapEx Required (USD) | India Government Share (50%) | Private / Foreign JV Share | YAROK14 Savings Equivalent |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 28 nm (in progress) | $11B | $5.5B | $5.5B | ~4 years at 5L site optimistic |
| 16–7 nm | $18B | $9B | $9B | ~6 years at 5L site optimistic |
| 3–5 nm | $25B | $12.5B | $12.5B | ~8 years at 5L site optimistic |
| 2 nm | $30B | $15B | $15B | ~10 years at 5L site optimistic |
| 1.4 nm | $48B | $24B | $24B | ~15 years at 5L site optimistic |
| **1 nm** | **$55–70B** | **$27.5–35B** | **$27.5–35B** | **~20 years at 5L site optimistic** |

**Reality check:** No single nation funds a 1nm fab from a single source. The US CHIPS Act committed $52.7B for the entire semiconductor ecosystem. India's ISM 1.0 committed ₹76,000 crore ($9.1B). A 1nm fab requires a **coalition model**: government subsidy (50%) + anchor foundry partner (TSMC/Samsung/Intel) + sovereign wealth fund + institutional debt.

### G.2 The TSMC Partnership Model — What It Takes

TSMC's decision to locate in Phoenix triggered a rapid influx of Tier-1 suppliers — Edwards Vacuum, EMD Electronics, and Chang Chun Arizona — each establishing local facilities. India's semiconductor parks should adopt this utilities-first model, pre-clearing environmental requirements, securing water and power commitments in writing, and incorporating infrastructure costs into the incentive structure.

For India to attract TSMC for a leading-edge fab partnership, it must offer:

| Requirement | Current India Status | Gap / Action Needed |
|---|---|---|
| 50% CapEx subsidy | ✅ Available via ISM | Extend to advanced nodes |
| Reliable 24/7 power (200–500 MW) | ⚠️ Partial | Dedicated grid for fab parks |
| Ultra-pure water (10M+ L/day) | ⚠️ Partial | UPW plants at Dholera scale |
| Talent pool (10,000 engineers) | ⚠️ Partial | IITB, IISc, NIT chip engineering push |
| Chemical and gas supply chain | ❌ Immature | ISM 2.0 + ECMS targets this |
| Logistics (port-to-fab) | ⚠️ Partial | Dholera SIR has connectivity |
| IP protection framework | ✅ Good (TRIPS compliant) | |
| Export control alignment | ✅ Quad member | Bilateral tech agreement needed |
| Tax incentives | ✅ Strong | State + central |
| Environmental clearances (fast-track) | ⚠️ Variable | Model on Dholera SIR experience |

### G.3 Financing Structure — 1nm India Fab

A realistic funding stack for a future India 1nm fab (total $55–70B over 15 years):

| Funding Source | Contribution | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| India Government (ISM 2.0/3.0) | $15–20B (25–30%) | Phased over 15 years |
| State Government (Gujarat/Andhra) | $5–8B (8–12%) | Land, water, power, state subsidy |
| Anchor Partner (TSMC/Samsung equity) | $12–18B (20–25%) | JV equity stake |
| Sovereign Wealth Fund (NIF/NIIF) | $8–12B (12–18%) | Long-term patient capital |
| Development Finance (ADB/World Bank) | $5–8B (8–12%) | Concessional rate |
| Private Equity / Institutional Debt | $5–10B (8–15%) | Commercial rate |
| YAROK14 National Savings (redirected) | Indirect — enables budget headroom | ₹1.25L cr/year frees sovereign capital |
| **Total** | **~$50–76B** | **Phased 2030–2045** |

## Section H — The YAROK14 MuP v2 ASIC Connection to India's Semiconductor Ecosystem

### H.1 YAROK14's Own Silicon Roadmap

YAROK14 is not just a beneficiary of India's semiconductor ecosystem — it is a contributor to it. The YAROK-14 MuP v2 custom ASIC (RTL complete in `vlsi_mup/`) is designed to replace the MSP430 + ESP8266 with a single custom chip:

| MuP v2 Parameter | Value |
|---|---|
| Process node target | SKY130B (130nm, open-source) / SCL India 180nm |
| FPGA prototype target | Lattice ECP5 / Xilinx Arty A7 |
| Core | PicoRV32 RISC-V (RV32IMC) |
| RTL status | Complete — 47 files, 6,700+ lines Verilog |
| Toolchain | 100% open-source (Yosys, OpenLane 2, Magic, Netgen) |
| Tapeout path | TinyTapeout (SKY130, ~$300–600) → SCL Mohali (180nm) → TSMC (mature node) |
| BOM saving vs discrete | ₹1,500 – ₹2,500 per unit |
| At 10,000 units | ₹1.5 – ₹2.5 crore saved per year |

### H.2 How YAROK14's ASIC Fits India's Semiconductor Journey

| Stage | YAROK14 MuP Action | India Semiconductor Ecosystem Benefit |
|---|---|---|
| Now | Tapeout at TinyTapeout / SKY130 | Validates RISC-V + custom peripheral on silicon |
| 2027 | FPGA prototype (ECP5) | Proven design ready for SCL Mohali |
| 2028 | SCL Mohali 180nm tapeout | Demonstrates ISM-funded domestic fab capability |
| 2030 | Mature TSMC node (28nm via Tata–PSMC) | First Made-in-India YAROK14 chip at commercial volume |
| 2032+ | Advanced node (7nm) for power efficiency | YAROK14 chips made in India's first 7nm fab |

> YAROK14's MuP v2 is designed to be the **first real-world IoT control ASIC taped out through India's ISM-funded fab ecosystem** — from SCL Mohali modernisation (₹4,500 crore, announced November 2025) to Tata–PSMC Dholera.

## Section I — Full Integrated Financial Summary

### I.1 YAROK14 Biomethane → India Semiconductor: Numbers in One Table

| Metric | Value |
|---|---|
| **YAROK14 small site savings** | ₹30,000 – ₹1.2 lakh/year |
| **YAROK14 institutional site savings** | ₹1.5 – ₹4 lakh/year |
| **National gross savings at 1L sites** | ₹6,000 – ₹25,000 crore/year |
| **National net savings at 1L sites (after CAPEX + OPEX)** | ₹2,500 – ₹12,000 crore/year |
| **National savings at 5L sites** | ₹30,000 – ₹1.25 lakh crore/year |
| **YAROK14 company revenue at 1,000 sites** | ₹15 – ₹18 crore |
| **YAROK14 company revenue at 10,000 sites** | ₹150 – ₹400+ crore |
| | |
| **ASML High-NA EUV price per unit** | $350M – $400M |
| **ASML Hyper-NA EUV (2030+)** | $700M – $724M+ |

| **YAROK14 MuP v2 at SCL Mohali** | ₹50–₹200 lakh (estimated prototype run) |

### I.2 The Single Most Important Strategic Insight

**India's path to 1nm is not a technology problem. It is a capital allocation, talent, and time problem.**

The technology will be commercially available and exportable to India within the timeframe India needs it (2035–2045). ASML will ship High-NA EUV to India. TSMC has demonstrated willingness to partner internationally. The US Quad framework actively supports India gaining semiconductor capability.

**What bridges the gap:**
1. National savings (from programmes like YAROK14) freeing sovereign capital
2. ISM 1.0 → 2.0 → 3.0 policy continuity
3. Phased node progression (28nm → 7nm → 2nm → 1nm, not a shortcut)
4. Anchor partner strategy (TSMC JV is the model)
5. Domestic ASIC ecosystem (YAROK14 MuP, DLI startups, IIT chip labs)
6. Talent pipeline (10,000 process engineers needed)

### I.3 ROI Comparison: Biomethane vs Semiconductor

| Investment | CapEx | Annual Return | ROI | Payback | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| YAROK14 small site (subsidised) | ₹39,750 | ₹17,800 | 44.8% | 2.25 years | Low |
| YAROK14 institutional (optimised) | ₹3,75,000 | ₹2,80,000 | 74.7% | 1.3 years | Low–Medium |
| India 28nm fab (Tata–PSMC) | $11B | $2–3B est. | 18–27% | 4–6 years | Medium |
| India 7nm fab (future) | $20B | $5–7B est. | 25–35% | 3–4 years | Medium–High |
| India 1nm fab (2040) | $60B | $12B+ | 20%+ | 5 years | High |
| TSMC 1.4nm (Fab 25, Taiwan) | $48.5B | $15B+ projected | 30%+ | 3–4 years | Low (TSMC) |

> **The pattern:** ROI at leading edge is excellent once yield matures — but the capital at risk and the time-to-profitability are enormous. India's 28nm fab is the right first step, with the ROI on subsidised terms being very attractive. Each subsequent node builds the talent, ecosystem, and yield knowledge needed for the next.

---

## Section J — Practical Steps: What India Must Do Now

### J.1 Immediate (2026–2028)

1. **Commission Tata–PSMC Dholera fab** on schedule — 28nm volume production by 2028
2. **Modernise SCL Mohali** (₹4,500 crore approved) — domestic government fab for defence and space
3. **Scale DLI scheme** — 23 projects sanctioned; target 200+ by 2028
4. **Negotiate TSMC 7nm JV** — use Dholera success as proof of execution capability
5. **Build UPW + power infrastructure** for advanced fab parks (Dholera SIR model)
6. **YAROK14 MuP v2 tapeout** at SCL Mohali — demonstrate Indian ASIC design → Indian fab

### J.2 Medium-Term (2028–2035)

1. **Launch ISM 2.0** — focused on equipment, materials, EDA tools, R&D centres
2. **Attract TSMC or Samsung** for a 7nm fab in India (JV, 50% ISM + 20% state)
3. **Build chip design talent pipeline** — 10,000 process engineers through IIT/IISc/NIT partnerships
4. **Negotiate ASML EUV supply agreement** — India as a strategic partner in ASML's customer base
5. **Launch India Semiconductor Sovereign Fund** — patient capital, 20-year horizon
6. **ECMS** — build chemicals, gases, photoresists, CMP slurry supply domestically

### J.3 Long-Term (2035–2045)

1. **2nm fab** — full domestic production with TSMC-equivalent partner
2. **High-NA EUV acquisition** — first units for R&D and then production
3. **1nm risk production** — targeting 2040–2042
4. **1nm volume production** — 2043–2045
5. **India as global foundry** — serving domestic AI/defence demand + export

## Section K — Reference: Key Semiconductor Financial and Technical Terms

| Term | Definition | YAROK14 / India Fab Context |
|---|---|---|
| **Wafer** | Thin silicon disc (~300mm) on which chips are patterned | 50,000 wpm = fab capacity target |
| **wpm** | Wafers per month — primary fab capacity metric | 50,000 wpm = large advanced fab |
| **Node / Process Node** | Transistor feature size (nm) — smaller = more powerful | 28nm (India now) → 1nm (India 2040) |
| **Yield** | % of dies per wafer that pass quality tests | Critical to profitability; TSMC mature node: 90%+ |
| **CapEx** | Capital Expenditure — fab construction + equipment | $55–70B for a 1nm greenfield |
| **OpEx** | Operating Expenditure — running cost | $3.5–7B/year for a 1nm fab |
| **TAM** | Total Addressable Market | Global semiconductor market: $1 trillion by 2030 |
| **EUV** | Extreme Ultraviolet Lithography — key to advanced nodes | $220M per Low-NA unit; $380M for High-NA |
| **High-NA EUV** | Numerical Aperture 0.55 — enables sub-2nm | Required for 1nm; India needs ~2035 |
| **DUV** | Deep Ultraviolet — mature lithography | For 28nm–90nm; India Phase 1 tool |
| **ASML** | Sole global supplier of EUV machines | TSMC/Samsung/Intel dependency; now India too |
| **Foundry** | Contract chip manufacturer (TSMC model) | India's target model — fab-for-hire |
| **OSAT** | Outsourced Semiconductor Assembly and Test | India's current phase — Micron, CG Power, Kaynes |
| **ATMP** | Assembly, Test, Mark, Package | Same as OSAT — India's ISM entry point |
| **Fabless** | Chip design without owning a fab | India has strength here — AMD, NXP design centres |
| **IDM** | Integrated Device Manufacturer (Intel model) | Design + fab + package — rare, capital-intensive |
| **ISM** | India Semiconductor Mission — MeitY nodal agency | Up to 50% CapEx subsidy for approved fabs |
| **DLI** | Design Linked Incentive — for fabless startups | 50% of design costs reimbursed |
| **SCL** | Semiconductor Complex Limited, Mohali | India's only domestic fab (legacy); ₹4,500 cr upgrade |
| **PSMC** | Powerchip Semiconductor Manufacturing Corp | Taiwan foundry — Tata's partner for 28nm |
| **DSCR** | Debt Service Coverage Ratio | Must be >1.2 for fab project debt |
| **IRR** | Internal Rate of Return | 18–28% for a mature 1nm fab |
| **NPV** | Net Present Value | Strongly positive at 1nm if yield and pricing hold |
| **Tapeout** | Final step of chip design — sending to fab for manufacturing | YAROK14 MuP v2: TinyTapeout → SCL → TSMC |
| **RTL** | Register Transfer Level — hardware design language (Verilog) | YAROK14 MuP v2 RTL: 6,700+ lines, complete |
| **PDK** | Process Design Kit — fab's design rules | SKY130B (open-source), SCL 180nm, TSMC N5 |
| **GDS / GDSII** | Chip layout file sent to fab for mask making | Final output of YAROK14 MuP OpenLane flow |
| **Lithography** | Process of printing circuit patterns onto wafers | ASML's monopoly product |
| **Photoresist** | Light-sensitive chemical applied to wafers | Key consumable; ₹300–600M/year for large fab |
| **CMP** | Chemical Mechanical Planarization — surface flattening | Between each metal layer; high consumable cost |
| **UPW** | Ultra-Pure Water — used in every wash step | 10M+ litres/day for a large fab |
| **Cleanroom** | ISO Class 1–3 environment — <1 particle/m³ | $3–5B civil cost for a 1nm fab |
| **Moore's Law** | Transistor density doubles every ~2 years | Still roughly holds; slowing below 2nm |
| **FinFET** | 3D transistor design — used at 7nm to 3nm | Replaces planar CMOS used at 28nm |
| **GAA / Nanosheet** | Gate-All-Around — transistor design for 2nm and below | TSMC A14/A10 uses 2nd-gen nanosheet |
| **TSMC Arizona cost premium** | Construction 4–5× more expensive than Taiwan | India is ~15–25% more expensive than Taiwan |

---
